  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_5f7763fd-0ff6-4f3a-beed-b8de75451af6'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

  <span id="freeText13751430247454653861" style="display:none">Aside from her dad, who passed away when she was six, Cassidy Jameson has only ever trusted one man: her best friend, Tyler. So of course she follows him to Texas when he leaves for college. She just didn't expect to be so drawn to their new roommate, Gage, a gorgeous guy with a husky Southern drawl. The only problem? He's Tyler's cousin.<br /><br />Gage Carson was excited to share an apartment off campus with his cousin. He didn't mind that Tyler was bringing the mysterious friend he'd heard about since they were kids ... until the most beautiful girl he's ever seen jumps out of his cousin's Jeep. There's something about Cassi that makes Gage want to give her everything. Too bad Tyler has warned him that she's strictly off-limits.<br /><br />Despite everything keeping them apart, Cassi and Gage dance dangerously close to the touch they're both been craving. But when disaster sends her running into Tyler's arms, Cassi will have to decide whether to face the demons of her past ... or to burn her chance at a future with Gage.</span>

<div id="review_449082757" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/449082757" />
    <a title="Ava" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5832186-ava"><img alt="Ava" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/449082757?book_show_action=true">Nov 05, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ava" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ava" href="/user/show/5832186-ava">Ava</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780062267719" href="/book/show/16075994-from-ashes">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5832186-ava?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5832186-ava?shelf=one-star">one-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5832186-ava?shelf=abandoned">abandoned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5832186-ava?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5832186-ava?shelf=realistic-fiction-romance">realistic-fiction-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5832186-ava?shelf=new-adult">new-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5832186-ava?shelf=creepy-love-interest">creepy-love-interest</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer449082757&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer449082757" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17567304008916958911"><i>This review contains <b>unmarked spoilers</b>.</i><br/><br/>TAKING CHANCES and Oceana are not friends.<br/><br/>We are not friends at all.<br/><br/>Not because that plot twist completely <i>crushed my heart</i>, or because the main character didn't end up with whom every one wanted. It was because I purely and truly despised that book, and for some crazy, unexplainable reason, I decided to read FROM ASHES. <br/><br/>In all honesty, I was hoping it would be be much better than its predecessor, so I could write a nice review instead of a incoherent, angr</span>
  <span id="freeText17567304008916958911" style="display:none"><i>This review contains <b>unmarked spoilers</b>.</i><br><br>TAKING CHANCES and Oceana are not friends.<br><br>We are not friends at all.<br><br>Not because that plot twist completely <i>crushed my heart</i>, or because the main character didn't end up with whom every one wanted. It was because I purely and truly despised that book, and for some crazy, unexplainable reason, I decided to read FROM ASHES. <br><br>In all honesty, I was hoping it would be be much better than its predecessor, so I could write a nice review instead of a incoherent, angry, babbling rant. I didn't expect much, but a girl can dream.<br><br>And once in a while, one shall stumble across a book that makes their blood boil and their vision red. It was unfortunate that for me, I found several books like that this year. But both of Ms. McAdam's books were near the top of 2012's fume list.<br><br><b>Synopsis</b><br><br>Cassidy Jameson has been physically, mentally, and emotionally abused by her mother and stepfather since her father's death. It is a secret that she keeps completely under lock and key, but there is one person that knows: her best friend, Tyler, who takes care of her when she is hurt and who has been Cass's crutch for years. <br><br>Tyler takes Cassidy with him to Texas when he attends college, and there she meets his cousin, Gage. It's practically love at first site for these two, but Tyler successfully keeps them apart... for a while, until shit hits the fan and blows the fuck up.<br><br><b>RETURN OF THE RICH BEAUTIFUL WHITE PEOPLE IN COMPLICATED LOVE PENTAGONS</b><br><br>I need my Aspirin, please.<br><br>First of all, Cassidy being abused does not belong in this book. It's just a plot device to give Cassidy a problem in life since she has none, a reason to be 'broken', to let Tyler take care of her, and to allow Gage to protect her and eventually end up with her. You could have removed the parts of the book where Cassidy talks about how she's been abused, and it will not have changed <i>in the least.</i> Because in the end, it's not a story about a shattered character who needs some TLC. It's pure love triangle - or actually, a near fucking <i>pentagon</i> - and shoving in a background of abuse in this story is total crap and absolutely out of place. <br><br>You know what's a real love story with a tortured main character? <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10194514.Pushing_the_Limits__Pushing_the_Limits___1_" title="Pushing the Limits (Pushing the Limits, #1) by Katie McGarry" rel="nofollow noopener">Pushing the Limits</a>.<br><br>Anyway, model-handsome Tyler drags Cassidy to Texas, where she meets his <i>hotter</i> cousin Gage (who even knew it was possible to get sexier than Tyler, right?), who, of course, is completely godly and charming and handsome and angelic and unearthly and <i>oh shut the fuck up.</i><br><br>You thought you knew insta-love? Hahaha, bitch, you're wrong. These two lay eyes on each other and it's a total nuclear explosion. But what attracts them in the first place? How beautiful they both are, of course! You can't have average or even pretty-looking characters in these books. They've all got to be the most stunning white people in the world.<br><br>I mean, they look better together than Ian Somerhalder and Nina Dobrev!<s>which is totally not fucking possible</s><br><br>So while Cassi here is having an orgasm looking at Gage, some chick wraps her arm around Gage and Cassidy, who hasn't even, you know, talked to Gage, starts to get annoyed and angry and even thinks about <i>plotting to destroy their relationship.</i><br><br>Says the girl who pages before, claimed that she didn't trust men.<br><br>OH MY GODS SERIOUSLY WHAT THE FUCK IS THIS<br><br>This is what Gage says on page thirteen, after meeting Cassidy. HE JUST MET HER, OKAY? I don't give two shits if there was 'electricity'. Electricity my ass. <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"... I'd already pictured her beneath me."</i>
</blockquote><br>He goes on to say how the wind was knocked out of him when he imagined Tyler and Cassi together.<br><br>THIS IS CREEPY NO ONE NEEDS SOME RANDOM FUCKER THINKING ABOUT HAVING SEX WITH YOU AND MAKING THEIRS YOURS OKAY STOP IT NOW IT AIN'T SEXY<br><br>Tyler manipulates Cassidy and Gage so they can never properly establish a romantic relationship - always ending up with Cassidy or Gage storming off and coming back in several months. However, Tyler blackmails Cassidy into being his girlfriend, or he'll bring her back to her abusive household and she'll <i>loose him</i>. Cassidy accepts.<br><br><a href="http://media.photobucket.com/image/what%20are%20you%20doing%20gifs/delaythedecay/Gifs/whatareyoudoing.gif?o=1" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380396598ra/764676.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>THIS BITCH NEEDS A SASSY GAY FRIEND.<br><br>Who the actual <i>fuck</i> would even <i>want</i> to stay with an asshole who would blackmail and threaten and manipulate you for SEX? <br><br>Later, Tyler nearly forces Cassidy to have sex with him, and when she doesn't, he pulls a Travis and comes home with a promiscuous girl (who just had sex with Gage, because without Cassi he's sexually frustrated) and then KICKS CASSIDY OUT IN THE FUCKING SNOW AND SHE ALMOST FREAKING DIES BEFORE GAGE SAVES HER<br><br>(but later they're friends again, don't worry)<br><br>Gage beats Tyler up, Cassi and Gage get together, butterflies poop rainbows and puppies fly. This should be the end, right? It's been a long ride, anyway.<br><br>NOPE, BECAUSE THESE BOOKS JUST DRAG THIS SHIT OUT. Pages and pages and endless chapters of absolutely nothing happening except Gage and Cassidy fuzzy and sexy time - WAIT I HAVE SPOTTED A DRAMA LLAMA, CASSIDY YOU STUPID BITCH, GET OVER YOURSELF BECAUSE HE HAS SEX WITH OTHER GIRLS TOO, NOT YOUR PURE WHITE VIRGIN ASS -<br><br><a href="http://media.photobucket.com/image/drama%20llama/boofy2010/funny/drama_llama.jpg?o=9" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380396598i/764677.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Finally, Cassidy leaves Texas and goes back home because her house has burned down, killing her stepfather and mother, who left her a suicide note and an 'apology' . She also meets detective Connor Green (he's <i>achingly handsome</i>!), with who she has a 'connection' with.<br><br><i>Connection</i>: in less than two weeks, Cassidy is making out with Connor (wait, I thought she had a boyfriend?) and going on and on about how she lurvs Gage, but Connor just <i>understands</i> her because he's been abused too, and oh, why can't she just have the best of both?<br><br><a href="http://media.photobucket.com/image/shut%20up%20gifs/dandy_monkey/gifs/hpshutup.gif?o=35" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380396598ra/764678.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Anyhow, she goes back to Texas, has a lot of sex with Gage in the house that they bought together, and then Connor comes back to confess that he 'needs' Cassidy (<i>"I need you,"</i>) but she brushes off the horny son of a bitch and tells him to go home. Then, like the rabbits they are, Gage and Cassi screw in more sexy places. Like on their kitchen island.<br><br>Watch out, innocent children! Stay out of that kitchen!<br><br>Cassidy and Gage get married less than two months later because marriage is the most important thing in the world to them, and it must be done immediately. Who cares that Cassidy isn't even old enough to legally drink a beer? NO ONE, CAUSE LOVE MEANS MARRIAGE, RIGHT?<br><br>Then Cassidy gets stung by a scorpion and I finally was like HELL YES IS THIS WHAT I'VE BEEN WAITING FOR? <br><br>But, alas, she survives (what else?) and it turns out she's already preggers (saw this coming from a fucking mile away) and then suddenly it's years later, and Cassidy has her baby, and another baby, and she's pregnant with her third child. You find out she and her second baby almost died in delivery - her heart literally stopped and started again.<br><br><a href="http://media.photobucket.com/image/are%20you%20fucking%20kidding%20me%20gifs/NASCAR_baby/GIFS/tumblr_lrshpier5L1qdjxpm.gif?o=0" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380396598ra/764679.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><i>Hey, I used this guy in my TAKING CHANCES review!</i><br><br>But seriously? She had to almost freaking die? AGAIN? That is such crap!<br><br><b>Characters</b><br><br>Cassidy is like this Chihuahua I know called Fifi. She's tiny, stupid, and constantly shaking in fear for no reason. Oh, and a serious damsel in distress. I have almost literally never encountered a heroine who was just so naive and empty and freaking idiotic. I wanted to grab her by the nonexistent balls and fling her around until the parts of her brain settled into the right places. <br><br>Being apparently abused is not an excuse to be such a moron, because trust me: Cassidy does not act like an abused person (nor does she think about it), and Echo from PUSHING THE LIMITS was also abused and she is far from idiot.<br><br>Here she is, calling all these girls sluts and shit, and meanwhile she's playing <i>three</i> guys before adding a couple more to the mix. Those girls aren't sluts, but she's kind of a cheater.<br><br>She is also gorgeously perfect, and beautiful, and supposed to be the girl all the guys want (there are over <i>seven</i> guys that wuv her). Supposedly she's delicate, sweet, and soft-spoken, ALL THE GUYS get into a fight over her, and she's constantly being saved from attempted rape or assault because of how hot she is. But there are no redeeming qualities about her except that she's a 'sandwich making bitch'.<br><br>The reason for Cassidy not telling anyone that she's being domestically abused is ridiculous. It's not that she's afraid, or her stepfather and mother have convinced her that no one will listen, or that they've just plainly scarred her. <i>She doesn't want them to 'take her away from Tyler'.</i> <br><br><a href="http://photobucket.com/images/moron%20gifs" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380396598ra/764680.gif" alt="Are you a Moron? Pictures, Images and Photos" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>I don't think she realizes that she is about to turn eighteen, and that they're not going to throw her in an asylum for the rest of her life. She's not going to loose shit.<br><br>And then, while Tyler shoves her onto a bed and starts kissing her roughly, I'M SO SERIOUS, they're like:<br><br><blockquote>
<i>"Tyler, you know I love you!"<br>"But you don't. Not the way I love you. Romantically."</i> *humps*<br><i>"Wh-what? But you only like me as a friend! I don't understand!</i> *shoves his tongue down her throat*<br><i>"I want you!</i>"<br><i>"Tyler, are you okay? We're just friends, and you know that."</i><br>*continues humping her*</blockquote><br>You must be completely STUPID to not realize they don't like you as a friend anymore. And, hey, when a guy dumps you, it's way worse than being forced to have a sexual and romantic relationship with someone, right?<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"It wasn't like my Tyler at all, and I was surprised by how much it hurt. It wasn't anything like when Gage broke my heart, but it still felt like someone had punched me in the stomach."</i>
</blockquote><br><br><a href="http://media.photobucket.com/image/fml%20gifs/ontdforkari/gifs/tumblr_lh7i81c86w1qe8a0fo1_500.gif?o=36" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380396598ra/764681.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>She annoyed me to no end, and the fact that not a single person gave a shit when she went around making out with everybody infuriated me. She was so dumb and plain, I just really, really wanted to bang my head against a wall.<br><br>Or, er, maybe introduce her to this guy:<br><br><a href="http://media.photobucket.com/image/american%20psycho%20gifs/professorbrackets/Gifs%20-%20Celebratory/americanpsycho.gif?o=12" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380396598ra/764682.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>But I'll spare you, Cassidy, because being head-desk-inducing doesn't deserve the fate you'll get with this American Psycho.<br><br>Gage is such a boring, possessive piece of plank wood. The only thing he was good for was sex and telling everyone that Cassidy was <i>his property</i>. I have nothing to say about him except that he needs to get his dick under control, because he got a boner every chapter or so looking at her. I will never call my friends 'darlings' again, because he completely ruined it for me and I hated his character, who always needed to pick Cassidy up and save her.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"I could claim you as mine."</i>
</blockquote><br>WE ARE NOT SLAVES YOU ASSHOLE.<br><br>Tyler is a blackmailing, threatening, manipulative fuckface and the fact that his blackmail is completely written off and forgiven is despicable and disgusting. There was nothing attractive about all the shit he pulled and I hope he gets hit by a truck and dies.<br><br>Connor is boring and blah, and he has no respect for Cassidy, who already has a boyfriend. The other characters were bland and lifeless and bored the shit out of me. Cassidy's stepfather and mother were sickening people and I'm not sorry they both burned to a crisp.<br><br>I didn't connect with any of the characters and the development was awful.<br><br><b>Romance and Stuff</b><br><br>Don't even get me started on this bullshit. Gage and Cassidy are one of the fastest insta-love relationships I've ever read, and in between it's eye-rolling angst that I didn't care for.<br><br>All the people falling head over heels for Cassidy got really old, really fast. She's always complaining about everyone being in love with her, and it really. pissed. me. off.<br><br><blockquote>
<i>"How was it possible to be so completely in love with someone but have this kind of chemistry with someone else at the same time?"</i> </blockquote><br>Go on, Cassidy. Please. Keep on whining while you're making out with Connor. You're suuuuchhhh a likable character, so we don't mind your constant bitching!<br><br><a href="http://photobucket.com/images/kill%20it%20gifs" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380396598ra/764683.gif" alt="kill myself Pictures, Images and Photos" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Everyone in the story is a beautiful rich white person, and when Cassidy didn't have any money because her mother took it, guess what? SHE GOT DA MONIES FROM THE WEALTHY-ASS FAMILY OF TYLER AND GAGE, because no white people love story can have a lack of money to do the things they want!<br><br>There was not one black person in FROM ASHES, or any person that wasn't white, for that matter. <br><br>And getting married in FROM ASHES is a must. It doesn't matter that they're still young and have a full life ahead of them. Marriage is the most important thing, and once that's over with, you can get pregnant and have a bunch of babies, and <i>then</i> you're allowed to live. Cassidy, like Harper, got pregnant before she was twenty-two, because children can't wait.<br><br><b>Writing</b><br><br>The writing in this is terrible. FROM ASHES has several transitions - one page, you'll be in present time, and the next, it's eight months later and you wouldn't even have realized it. There are way too many time changes and it needs to slow down.<br><br>On a scale of one to Snuggie, how unnecessary is most of the stuff in FROM ASHES?<br><br>More useless than an <a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Z86V_ICUCD4" rel="nofollow noopener">On/Off machine.</a><br><br>There is also so much useless, needless shit in these books that should've been taken out a long time ago. I thought this was what an editor was for? FROM ASHES should've finished when Cassidy started a steady relationship with Gage instead of dragging us by the hair for another two hundred effing pages of drama, stupid shit, and the epilogue. Leave something to the imagination, gosh! Stop giving your characters a complete future. <br><br>Cassidy getting stung by a scorpion? ARE YOU SERIOUS? This should have been an extra scene edited out! It's not important to the story! <br><br>I don't think McAdams realized how many times Gage's pants started tightening. It was ridiculous. That boy has some problem with his penis. It needs to be checked out. And I'm tired of hearing about Cassidy's whiskey/amber/honey/piss colored eyes. WE GET THE FUCKING POINT. WE KNOW.<br><br>And remember my rant about how people's eyes don't automatically 'darken' like a fucking lamp switch? Well, way more eye-darkening here! I'm starting to think they're all closeted vampires.<br><br><a href="http://media.photobucket.com/image/damon%20gifs/nbaringer12/GIFS/DAMONVALUES.gif?o=8" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380396598ra/764684.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><i>Damon Salvator, c'mon down, my sexy friend!</i><br><br>The dialogue was so choppy and the writing itself is simple to read, yet amateur and not good at all. Complete pain in the ass.<br><br><b>Wrap-up</b><br><br>I hated this book with a burning, fiery passion. It angered me and I hope that no girl actually admires Cassidy's cheating behavior and misogynistic ways.</span>

<div id="review_406894326" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/406894326" />
    <a title="Elizabeth (Liz)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5495317-elizabeth-liz"><img alt="Elizabeth (Liz)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1551206872p2/5495317.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/406894326?book_show_action=true">Sep 03, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elizabeth (Liz)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elizabeth (Liz)" href="/user/show/5495317-elizabeth-liz">Elizabeth (Liz)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/15980171-from-ashes">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5495317-elizabeth-liz?shelf=ebook-read">ebook-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5495317-elizabeth-liz?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5495317-elizabeth-liz?shelf=5-star-reads">5-star-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5495317-elizabeth-liz?shelf=contemporary-romance-read">contemporary-romance-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5495317-elizabeth-liz?shelf=ya-new-adult-read">ya-new-adult-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5495317-elizabeth-liz?shelf=ebook-edelweiss-read">ebook-edelweiss-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer406894326" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2338348324251733339">Review posted at: <a href='http://sweptawaybyromance.blogspot.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Swept Away By Romance</a><br/><br/><br/>Genre: New Adult<br/><br/>Heat Level: Moderately Steamy<br/><br/>Angst Level: Angsty, but not OTT (nothing which will require you to seek a support group)<br/><br/>Crazy-Dayzzz Drama Level: Nothing OTT <br/><br/>Possible Issues For Peeps: Some discussion of abuse<br/><br/><br/><br/>5 Stars<br/><br/><br/>A star was born with Taking Chances--one of my favorite books of 2012--and, with the release of From Ashes, Molly McAdams continues to shine so very, VERY bright!! <br/><br/>Cassidy Jameson escapes a wretched, abusive existence in California</span>
  <span id="freeText2338348324251733339" style="display:none">Review posted at: <a href="http://sweptawaybyromance.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Swept Away By Romance</a><br /><br /><br />Genre: New Adult<br /><br />Heat Level: Moderately Steamy<br /><br />Angst Level: Angsty, but not OTT (nothing which will require you to seek a support group)<br /><br />Crazy-Dayzzz Drama Level: Nothing OTT <br /><br />Possible Issues For Peeps: Some discussion of abuse<br /><br /><br /><br />5 Stars<br /><br /><br />A star was born with Taking Chances--one of my favorite books of 2012--and, with the release of From Ashes, Molly McAdams continues to shine so very, VERY bright!! <br /><br />Cassidy Jameson escapes a wretched, abusive existence in California with her life-long best friend Tyler by her side when he literally packs her up and moves her with him to college in Texas. They share a bond that most don't understand and many mistake for something more than friendship. Tyler and her deceased father are the only two people Cassidy has put her trust in for the majority of her life. She has absolutely no one else in her life, because she has never allowed anyone other than Tyler into her reality. Cassidy depends thoroughly and completely on Tyler to meet the few emotional needs she has and to be her sole support system. When they arrive in Austin, TX, Cassidy immediately meets their new roommate, Tyler's cousin, Gage Carson. From the first meeting Cassidy and Gage are inexplicably and strongly drawn to one another. To Gage, Cassidy is the most beautiful girl he has ever seen. She is quiet and kind, a phenomenal cook, wise beyond her years, a survivor, and he knows she carries a great deal of pain. To Cassidy, Gage is the single best looking guy she's ever met. He's equal parts city and country, has a drawl to die for, is a true gentleman, and has an amazing family. Neither understands the strength of the attraction between them. Gage has never experienced this immediate, imperative need to protect a girl, to make her his in every way. Because of her background, Cassidy does not trust easily or quickly, nor has she ever felt quite this kind of pull toward a man. Due to manipulation by Tyler, both Cassidy and Gage dance around their feelings for one another for a year and a half, both taking somewhat drastic measures to try and forget one another. However, the day finally comes when Tyler drives Cassidy straight into the arms of Gage, and both Cassidy and Gage decide they are finally ready to take a chance on being together. But, Cassidy still has a past to face and demons to fight. Are any of them strong enough to withstand the fallout? Is the love Gage and Cassidy have for each other enough to carry them through?<br /><br /><br />My God, does Molly McAdams know how to tell a story! From Ashes so completely and totally sucked me in, that I literally read it front to back, through the night, WITHOUT STOPPING!! This is the second book from this author, and the second book of hers that I've read in one sitting. There is something about the way she tells a story, writes a character. I literally have yet to be able to put one of her books down without finishing it! Molly's stories are compelling, emotional, sexy, exciting, fun and twisty. From Ashes is *exactly* that, in every way. I had such high hopes for this book, and she exceeded them. I became so utterly involved with and absorbed by the story and the characters, even when I found them thoroughly annoying and wanted to smack each of them upside the head!!! I simply could not put this book down until I knew how it ended. I dare you to try!<br /><br />Speaking of the ending, the epilogue is FABULOUS! I love a good epilogue, I admit it. And, I've been known to pitch a fit when A) there isn't ANY epilogue and/or B) the epilogue is less than stellar. Let me assure you, at about four this morning, I was doing the most obnoxious happy dance you would NEVER want to see! My cats eyed me with complete disdain;) But, that's just how much I LOVED this epilogue!<br /><br />A note to those who have read Taking Chances and were completely traumatized by a certain event in that story, I'm personally giving you the all-clear for From Ashes;) You may shed some tears, because, frankly, Molly's just that good, but you will NOT need therapy after this book:)<br /><br />Now, for my personal plea to Molly McAdams. When you read From Ashes--and YOU BETTER READ IT!--you will meet a character by the name of Detective Connor Green. If you are anything like me, you will join me in begging Molly McAdams for the following: PLEASE, PLEASE GIVE CONNOR GREEN A STORY...PRETTY PLEASE?!?!<br /><br />I &lt;3 you, Molly McAdams. To anyone reading this review, I just have to say: GO! RUN!! BUY. THE. BOOK!!!<br /><br /><br /><br /><br />**ARC courtesy of HarperCollins (William Morrow Paperbacks) via Edelweiss</span>

<div id="review_423003558" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/423003558" />
    <a title="Brenna" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12928663-brenna"><img alt="Brenna" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1580475762p2/12928663.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/423003558?book_show_action=true">Sep 27, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brenna" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brenna" href="/user/show/12928663-brenna">Brenna</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/15980171-from-ashes">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer423003558" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14540476914643686217">I have to start by saying that I <strong>really, really</strong> wanted to like this book. I was looking forward to it, I had been reading the teasers, I was excited. I read Taking Chances a few months ago and I loved it. There were things I had issues with in that book too, but I <em>wanted to</em> read it the entire time. I had to know. It actually got some (well a lot, let's not kid ourselves here) emotion out of me and I <strong>cared</strong>! By the end of From Ashes, I just didn't <strong>care</strong> anymore. <br/><br/>The story starts with Tyler & Cassi </span>
  <span id="freeText14540476914643686217" style="display:none">I have to start by saying that I <strong>really, really</strong> wanted to like this book. I was looking forward to it, I had been reading the teasers, I was excited. I read Taking Chances a few months ago and I loved it. There were things I had issues with in that book too, but I <em>wanted to</em> read it the entire time. I had to know. It actually got some (well a lot, let's not kid ourselves here) emotion out of me and I <strong>cared</strong>! By the end of From Ashes, I just didn't <strong>care</strong> anymore. <br /><br />The story starts with Tyler &amp; Cassi moving to Texas and within the first few pages you learn that Cassi has been <strong>severely</strong> abused every single day of her life for the past 11 years. At this point, my heart was totally breaking for this girl. I just kept thinking, "this girl better get her HEA after the hell she's been through." <br /><br />Then she meets Gage, Tyler's cousin. Gage was definitely the most redeeming part of this book. He was just yummy. I loved her description of him... <em>"...but he didn’t look like someone who spent hours in the gym or taking steroids. The only way I can describe them is natural, and labor-made."</em> So, like I said, yummy! He is also incredibly sweet, but not too sweet, a little rugged, and just all <em>man</em>. So anyways, immediately Gage is drawn to her and she to him. This is where the first sign of trouble was for me. They hadn't said two sentences to each other and he was already jealous of every person around her and acting a little obsessive. I get an initial attraction, but this was just annoying to me, even though I actually liked Gage. <br /><br />Things get complicated because Tyler is also in love with Cassi and has been "her rock" since she was six-years-old. He does everything he can to keep Cassi &amp; Gage from one another. He is just down right manipulative, deceitful, and just flat out <strong>unlikeable</strong>. If there had been parts in Tyler's POV or if he had just been upfront with his feelings or with his disapproval of Cassi &amp; Gage being together, I would have probably liked Tyler, but he acted like a little boy trying to hide his favorite toy. It was the sneaky underhanded way he went about keeping them apart that really got under my skin. And, the kicker, there is zero communication, so he gets away with it for waaaay too long. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Tyler eventually comes around and gets on board with their relationship and even helps them get together/back together, but it was way too little too late for me. He was so unlikeable at that point I couldn't even commend him on getting over his major douchey-ness in the first half. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Cassi &amp; Tyler's relationship was a hard one to wrap my head around. I loved that he was so there for her, but at the same time, some things just didn't add up. What bothered me is that Cassi was made to look like a complete idiot to not realize Tyler's feelings toward her. Woman are not stupid and oblivious to the effect they can have on others and that's how I felt here. <br /><br />There were way too many things going on, by the end I was just exhausted. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Let's count the love interests- WAY TOO MANY! Tyler, Gage, then there's Jesse who works with Cassi and wants her right off the bat too. Then there's this random detective thrown back in there who immediately falls in love with her too. And there mention of several other guys who want her and who Gage &amp; Tyler fight with over her.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I don't understand the need for more than two love interests max. I don't think anyone else in this story actually added anything to it or served a purpose. They could have just as easily been a friend or any other character. By making each person immediately wanting Cassi in a romantic way (and why did the want her again? I never got that either...) it just made it annoying and repetitive.<br /><br />There are many obstacles, struggles to deal with, and internal demons to face for these characters, but bottom line was I just didn't care by the end. I never felt a connection to any of the characters. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ The only moment I felt any real emotion was when Cassi gets the letter from her mother after she dies. That was a shining moment in this for sure.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> As "yummy" as Gage was, he even got on my nerves at times. I don't feel like the characters were ever properly developed. I was just craving some dialogue that would show personality and build the relationships without actually talking about the relationships. I just never felt it. With everything that Cassi went through, I did want her to have her HEA, don't get me wrong, I'm not heartless, but I just didn't care to hear how it happened. <br /><br />There were a few things I enjoyed and that was the whole ranch thing and Gage's family. They were entertaining and those were the moments I actually smiled and thought I could keep going. Gage's dad was a keeper...<em>"...argue with your mama, I sleep on the couch and she doesn’t feed me. So I don’t argue with your mama.” </em><br /><br />I can't remember a book in recent years that I struggled so much to finish. By the end I was so checked out. I read books because I enjoy them, not because I have to, and this book felt like a chore at some points. It's unfortunate because I actually think Molly McAdams can write and even though this was a definite miss for me, I'll keep an open mind and try out her work in the future. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14540476914643686217" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/465019860" />
    <a title="Ade" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5445524-ade"><img alt="Ade" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1595773125p2/5445524.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/465019860?book_show_action=true">Nov 27, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ade" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ade" href="/user/show/5445524-ade">Ade</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/15980171-from-ashes">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">No one. Seriously. No one.</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5445524-ade?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5445524-ade?shelf=why-would-anyone-write-this-book">why-would-anyone-write-this-book</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5445524-ade?shelf=banished-to-the-depths-of-hell">banished-to-the-depths-of-hell</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5445524-ade?shelf=cheating-is-not-cute">cheating-is-not-cute</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer465019860" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8799875888120389516"><b>EDIT 12/13/12:</b> I know, I know! I know I said I wouldn't review it but I can't help myself. The following is only one out of the many things that bothered me though, so this'll be short. <br/><br/>What the hell is it with McAdams and time frames? She basically DOES NOT USE THEM. It jumps from a week, to 8 months with no warning, and you're left going WTF? She really needs to work on this issue before she writes more books. There were times in the book when it jumped from one day, to 3 weeks later and it wa</span>
  <span id="freeText8799875888120389516" style="display:none"><b>EDIT 12/13/12:</b> I know, I know! I know I said I wouldn't review it but I can't help myself. The following is only one out of the many things that bothered me though, so this'll be short. <br /><br />What the hell is it with McAdams and time frames? She basically DOES NOT USE THEM. It jumps from a week, to 8 months with no warning, and you're left going WTF? She really needs to work on this issue before she writes more books. There were times in the book when it jumped from one day, to 3 weeks later and it wasn't clear until halfway through the chapter. It's annoying as heck and it made me want to scream.<br /><br /><br /><br /><b>EDIT 12/12/12:</b> I know I said I wasn't going to write a review, but I honestly feel that I can explain this book to you in ten simple steps. Ready for it?<br /><br /><br /><b>Step 1)</b> Innocent virgin leaves an unhappy home<br /><b>Step 2)</b> Innocent virgin meets hot bad boy <br /><b>Step 3)</b> Insta-love<br /><b>Step 4)</b> Something gets in the way of their being together, <br /><b>Step 5)</b> They struggle with the obstacle, but eventually their "love" overcomes it<br /><b>Step 5)</b> They get together *insert gasp here 'cause it's totally supposed to be this big exciting thing, right?*<br /><b>Step 6)</b> Innocent virgin turns into raging sexaholic<br /><b>Step 7)</b> Someone dies or gets pregnant, or maybe even both<br /><b>Step 8)</b> There is either extreme grief or happiness depending on which route the author took for step 7<br /><b>Step 9)</b> Another stupid obstacle that they overcome with their "love"<br /><b>Step 10)</b> They all live happily ever after.<br /><br />The best part about this wonderful little formula? It seems to apply to a large amount of the New Adult books being published! Isn't that just great?<br /><br /><br /><br /><br />I hated this book. I hated it even more than <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15739018.Taking_Chances" title="Taking Chances by Molly McAdams" rel="nofollow noopener">Taking Chances</a>. I honestly have nothing nice to say about this book, so I'll refrain from saying anything at all.</span>

<div id="review_465003770" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/465003770" />
    <a title="Lisbeth Avery {Domus Libri}" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8282085-lisbeth-avery-domus-libri"><img alt="Lisbeth Avery {Domus Libri}" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1426613564p2/8282085.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/465003770?book_show_action=true">Nov 27, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lisbeth Avery {Domus Libri}" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lisbeth Avery {Domus Libri}" href="/user/show/8282085-lisbeth-avery-domus-libri">Lisbeth Avery {Domus Libri}</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer465003770" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7594431124035543463"><b>This <s>review</s> rant will not be in normal format, instead it will be in freehand along with unmarked major spoilers.</b><br/><br/>I really shouldn't review this book. I really shouldn't. It's just going to make me angry, plus I have other books to review. But, books that make me so angry like FROM ASHES, I need to review, no matter how bad it is for my sanity.<br/><br/>FROM ASHES is pretty much the worst book I have ever read. I know I'm going to say it again and probably will till the end of time but at this time, I cann</span>
  <span id="freeText7594431124035543463" style="display:none"><b>This <s>review</s> rant will not be in normal format, instead it will be in freehand along with unmarked major spoilers.</b><br><br>I really shouldn't review this book. I really shouldn't. It's just going to make me angry, plus I have other books to review. But, books that make me so angry like FROM ASHES, I need to review, no matter how bad it is for my sanity.<br><br>FROM ASHES is pretty much the worst book I have ever read. I know I'm going to say it again and probably will till the end of time but at this time, I cannot imagine a worse book. The only reason I finished this piece of utter shit is because FROM ASHES is the most readable book ever. <br><br>Yes, I know, that makes no sense since I mentioned (once or twice) that I HATE this book but it's true. Molly McAdams has succeeded in making a book you hate to love to read (I'm pretty sure that's the first of its kind). I wanted to know what happened next even though I was literally <b>screaming</b> at the book. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I'm serious about that. I was screaming expletives at my kindle. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>The characters in this book are just terrible. I could go on forever but here is a basic summary:<br><br>Cassidy: Cheating, bitchy, judgmental girl who thinks she's better than everyone. One of the main characters whose only problems in life are: trying to decide which guy (out of 5 guys) she loves, handling a real life job, and being unable to have sex 10 times a day.<br><br>Gage: Boring, possessive, and bland all describe Gage. Me no like.<br><br>Tyler: THIS GUY IS WORSE THAN TRAVIS MADDOX. He is one of the worst love interests - no characters - I've ever encountered. Ever.<br><br>The plot of FROM ASHES makes absolutely no sense, at all. It was just terrible. In fact, I will recap the book's plot for your enjoyment/torture. Get ready guys because this is one messed up book.<br><br>The books starts off with Cassidy recounting how she's so scared and has so many problems. These problems range from bad to not being bad at all. The worst being <s>her parents abusing her as a kid</s> not being able to decide if she loves Tyler or Gage this week and the least being that she's too pretty.<br><br>I know, I know, it's so horrible.<br><br>Somehow, these abusive parents allow Cassidy to leave her home and travel to Texas. Note, this is realistic fiction and everyone knows that this is all very plausible. Anyway, she moves to Texas with her hot best friend (but he doesn't have aaanny romantic feeling towards her). There, she meets his even hotter (I know, I know, how is this possible?) cousin Gage. Let's examine some quotes now.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>What with Tyler's possessiveness and all no one even attempted to get close enough to me. Not that it bothered me...</i>
</blockquote><br>Cassidy says this after stating how Tyler could never like her romantically. Also, how can you be <i>okay</i> with this amount of obsessiveness.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>Gage was like a brother to him [Tyler] and Tyler hadn't seen him in a few years, so their sharing an apartment would be good for Ty.</i>
</blockquote><br>HAHA you can guess how long Tyler thinks of Gage as a brother instead of a rival.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>Tyler dropped my hand, only to put his on the small of my back as he led me over to Mr. New [Gage] and the leggy blonde.</i>
</blockquote><br>You just met Gage and you're already calling his girlfriend a "leggy blonde". <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"I'm Brynn [this is the leggy blonde], Gage's girlfriend." Her eyes narrowed.</i>
</blockquote><br>Woah, already jealous huh? Now the next few quotes are from Gage's point of view.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>All I could think about was closing the distance between us [Gage and Cassidy].</i>
</blockquote><br>You just met this girl a few hours ago. Slooooww down cowboy.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>I was frozen in place, taking in the most beautiful girl I'd ever seen.</i>
</blockquote><br>DUUDE you met her a few minutes ago.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>I couldn't even stop the growl that came from my throat when I saw it [Tyler holding Cassidy's hand].</i>
</blockquote><br>WHY ARE YOU GROWLING MAN? Staph kthanks.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>And yeah, I'm not gonna lie, I'd already pictures her beneath me.</i>
</blockquote><br>GAGE <br><br>WHAT<br><br>THE<br><br>FUCK<br><br>DUDE<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"She's mine Gage, Let's get that clear right now." [said Tyler]</i>
</blockquote><br>Dude, no. She's not.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"Damn, when you said your cousin was bringing a chick, I wasn't expecting her to be so hot," Jake said.<br>"Jake, touch her again.... see what fucking happens." [said Gage]</i>
</blockquote><br>Ok, so Gage is already threatening people to lay off "his woman". At 3%. <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>How was I already so into this girl that it physically hurt to think of her being with Ty?</i>
</blockquote><br>Trying to figure that one out myself honestly.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"she's been cooking for herself since she was six" [Ty on Cassidy]</i>
</blockquote><br>Why does the main female character always have to know how to cook and seem to be the only one who does?<br><br>Anyway, a bit more plot and then we'll go over quotes because I have the whole book highlighted (well pretty much all of it). The next 10% or so is Cassidy lusting over Gage's body while sincerely denying that Ty could ever love her all while Ty continually tells Gage that Cassidy is "his". At 10% in, Tyler forces himself onto Cassidy.<br><br>Before he does that, Tyler visits Gage. <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>I already hated thinking about what happened between Tyler and Cassidy, but having Tyler tell me he was about to go screw her made it that much worse. I'm sorry, not screw her, bang her. Like it was no big deal, just announced "I'm gonna go bang my girl." [from Gage's POV]</i>
</blockquote><br>God, what is wrong with Tyler? How could anyone <i>like</i> this guy? This is disgusting especially since this is coming from a guy who supposedly loves Cassidy like a sister. Just disgusting. <br><br>After that, Cassidy smartly decides not to sleep in Ty's room like she always did before. So what does she do? She sleeps on the couch and then lets Gage pick her up and put her on his bed. She's not even scared when she wakes up on the bed of some guy she met a few weeks ago.<br><br>A bunch of random and un-noteworthy things happen (including Cassidy's eighteenth birthday). Let's examine some of these quotes shall we?<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>... there was no doubt in my mind I was in love with Cassidy. [Gage's POV]</i>
</blockquote><br>First of all, what kind of sentence is <i>that</i>? I mean, does it make any sense to you? The second thing is that this is 12% into the book. Twelve percent and Gage is confessing his love.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>I loved everything about him.<br>I loved him.</i>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380398997ra/771631.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Sometimes, Sassy Gay Friend is the only way to express my feelings... *sigh*<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>I cook for six ridiculously obnoxious college guys while they take turns playing Xbox.</i>
</blockquote><br><br>Why? Why the fuck do you do is Cassidy? You say hate doing it yet you do.<br><br>Ok, back to boring plot summaries. Gage and Cassidy sort of, kind of get together then Cassidy does something and Gage gets all macho man angry and dumps her. Cassidy gets all depressed cause "O NOES HE DON'T LIKE MEH".<br><br>Then Cassidy meets Gage again and they make up. Somehow. I really have no idea how that happened. If anyone figured this out, I'd be happy to add it in. One chapter Gage is like "RAWR SHE HATE ME" and Cassidy is practically mirroring that feeling, and in the next?<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"Cassidy," I breathed.<br>She launched herself at me and wrapped her arms around my neck, whispering into y ear. "I missed you so much, Gage."</i>
</blockquote><br><br>Uhhh.... kthen.<br><br>In a few pages, Cassidy has already attracted another guy who tries to force her into having sex. All I can say is, girl get yo rape whistle out. Doing his Travis Maddox thing, Gage goes and breaks Max's nose. Why do love interests need to break people's noses? Is that cool or something?<br><br>Gage's pants get tighter a few <s>dozen</s> times and then Tyler tells Gage that Cassidy preformed oral sex to him and Gage goes insane. I think Tyler and Cassidy get together in this time but I'm not sure because Tyler kisses Cassidy all the time.<br><br>Like, pretty much every page but DON'T WORRY GUYS HE HAS NO ROMANTIC FEELINGS TOWARDS CASSIDY. <br><br>-.-<br><br>Cassidy get's a job and everything is quiet for a bit before (yep there's always a <i>before...</i>) TYLER TRIES TO FUCKING RAPE HER. This part made me so angry. It wasn't the worst part in the book but, god, it was close. This time, he doesn't do anything that bad, but just wait ok?<br><br>Gage gets pissed and goes out whoring. He brings home a couple of girls and has sex with them (but there was this funny moment when he screamed out CASSIDY during sex and got slapped). What happens on the next page?<br><br>Tyler tries to, more forcefully this time, rape her. This is where I'm going to share a few of the GRRRR quotes.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"You'll enjoy it, Cassi. I promise."</i>
</blockquote><br><br>Dear Tyler and other men out there, just because it's sex, doesn't mean people enjoy it. You are forcing yourself upon a girl and just because you think, "she'll like it", doesn't mean it's not RAPE. R. A. P. E. RAPE. <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"You want this, Cassi, don't tell me you don't. Your little moans and sighs, and damn it, Cassi, you're met as fuck. So why are you telling me to stop?" Tyler searched my face and shook his head slightly. "I swear to God, if you say you don't want this...."</i>
</blockquote><br><br>THIS IS A LOVE INTEREST PEOPLE. HE'S NOT THE ANTAGONIST, HE'S THE FREAKING LOVE INTEREST. This is just sick, ok? There is absolutely no excuse for rape, and out of all the ones people tell the victim, this is the worst.<br><br>No. Just no.<br><br>Now, what does our favorite love interest do after he stops humping her? He goes out, gets drunk, and brings home a girl to have sex with. WHAT WHAT WHAT. NO. This is NOT ok. Ever. NO. Why are these guys going all Travis on me?<br><br>Cassidy goes into a rage and Tyler kicks her out of the house without phone or proper clothes. Cassidy almost dies of hypothermia before being saved by the amazing, strong, wonderful Gage. Once she warms up, Gage yells at her telling her that he's mad at <i>her</i> for being kicked out and almost dying.<br><br>ARE YOU FREAKING KIDDING ME?!?<br><br>Nothing happens for a while (except for Cassidy's friend trying to get her to date someone even though she's stringing along two other guys). Gage tells Cassidy that he loves her and she goes too. They go through that "OMG I THOUGHT YOU WOULD NEVA WANT MEH?" conversation.<br><br>Gage and Cassidy have lots and lots of sex everywhere (bed, shower, couch, and the kitchen table) and he calls Cassidy his girl around 15 times. Jesse is introduced and he's in lurve with Cassidy as well. I'm still trying to figure out what they all see in her.<br><br>Cassidy cooks for some guys and this is what one of them say to her:<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"I want a damn SMB too! Doesn't matter if she thinks it's 'nothing fancy' or not, thee isn't another SMB out there like Cassi. That's it, I'm kidnapping and keeping her." Jake sounded exasperated.<br>"What the hell is a SMB?" Ethan asked, but we all looked confused.<br>Jake looked at us like we should know this already. "SMB? Sandwich-Making Bitch."</i>
</blockquote><br><br>What. The. Fuck.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/410425.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>But, wait, it gets better. <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>Cassidy was wiping tears from her eyes when her laughs turned into soft giggles ... "And I didn't take it as offensive. It's like that whole women-belong-in-the-kitchen-barefoot-and-pregnant thing; it's funny."</i>
</blockquote><br><br>GRRRRRR NO NO NO NO NO NO NO NO IT'S NOT FUNNY AT ALL. IT'S DEMEANING AND ENTIRELY UN-FUNNY. <br><br>After that, Cassidy basically turns into a sex addict and has sex everywhere. Gage hits some more people and accidentally hits Cassidy. She then finds out her old house had been burned down - yes, parent's house got burned down with them in it.<br><br>She leaves and meets Connor Green who she has an affair with. She then has the gall to confront Gage about his one night stand a few months ago. Whaaaa? Cassidy is also the one who says she doesn't trust guys.<br><br>Gage and Cassidy get together and Connor comes to ask Cassidy to go live with him. She declines and moves in with Gage. Turns out he made her a house and what do they do the moment they enter? Have sex. Then have more sex (ON THE KITCHEN ISLAND PEOPLE).<br><br>They get married; Cassidy almost dies (twice - scorpion bite and labor issues) and has three kids. The end. All I could get out by the end of the book was RAWR I HATE THIS. It was just terrible. Never, ever recommend. In fact run away.<br><br><br><i>Find this review and more <a href="http://assortedinsanityreviewers.blogspot.com" rel="nofollow noopener">at my blog</a>:</i><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380360324i/711186.png" width="150" height="150" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> </["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

</a><br/><br/><b>
  <i><br/>They've been best friends since they were seven. He was always there for her when she needed him. In her pain and in her heartache. He never let her down. EVER. Now it's time for him to go but there is no way he is leaving her behind.</i>
</b> <br/><br/><b>Good bye California, Hello Texas</b><br/>When Cassidy Jameson moves to Texas with her best friend Tyler she has no idea what to expect. After recently graduating high school she has no plans to further her e</span>
  <span id="freeText18237822578354447602" style="display:none">SPOILER FREE REVIEW<br>3 STARS out of 5<br>Genre: New Adult/College<br><br><a href="http://s1308.photobucket.com/albums/s607/aim4fashion/sexy%20couples/?action=view&amp;current=tumblr_mf3x2sEo0x1raly7do1_500.jpg" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380390530i/752264.jpg" alt="Photobucket" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>
  <i><br>They've been best friends since they were seven. He was always there for her when she needed him. In her pain and in her heartache. He never let her down. EVER. Now it's time for him to go but there is no way he is leaving her behind.</i>
</b> <br><br><b>Good bye California, Hello Texas</b><br>When Cassidy Jameson moves to Texas with her best friend Tyler she has no idea what to expect. After recently graduating high school she has no plans to further her education. So for now Tyler's plan to attend college and become roommates with his cousin Gage is now her plan too. Well minus the college part.<br><br><a href="http://s1308.photobucket.com/albums/s607/aim4fashion/?action=view&amp;current=tumblr_mcryilFFVW1r6xq40o1_500-1.jpg" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380390530i/752265._SY540_.jpg" alt="Photobucket" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>When they arrive in Texas they unpack and then head out to a party where Gage currently is in attendance with his friends. All Cassi really knows about Gage is that he grew up on a ranch and that he is two years older than her and Tyler. She gets out of Tyler's jeep expecting to see a laso carrying cowboy and gets no such thing. No, she gets a six foot dark haired sex god.<br><br><i>
  <b>The first night I met her, I felt her before I even saw her. It’s like I had to look up at her, and when I did . .  . I swear to God the world stopped moving.</b>
</i> ~Inner monologue of Gage<br><br> Before they are even introduced sparks are flying between Gage and Cassidy. And his southern charm has her completely drawn in. Unbeknownst to Cass the second she is off to mingle with party goers Tyler sets up position. He makes it clear to his cousin that Cassidy is his and off limits.<br><br><i>
  <b>“I couldn’t care less if you’re friends with her. Just don’t forget that I’m the one who’s been there for her every day for the last eleven years. Not you. I still see how you’re looking at her, I’m not fucking blind, Gage.”</b>
</i> ~Tyler<br><br><br>Neither Gage or Cassidy can resist the pull they feel towards each other. Yet Tyler's lies and deceit keep them apart for a year and a half until the night Tyler's pushy selfish ways send Cassi running to Gage. Literally.<br>After resisting one another they finally get a chance to talk and acknowledge how they feel. Weeks pass and they live in happiness untainted by Tyler... That is until an emergency sends Cassi not just back to Tyler but to California as well.<br><br><u>Fave Line</u><br><br><i>“How people can do that to their own kid is beyond me. People like that need to be arrested, or shot. I’m sure we can find some ditches.”</i> <br>~John<br><br><u>Fave Lines that made me laugh out loud</u><br><br><i>“Dad, is she serious?”</i> John shrugged. <br><i>“I argue with your mama, I sleep on the couch and she doesn’t feed me. So I don’t argue with your mama.”</i> ~Gage and his father John<br><br><i>"Your ranch is on Google, dumbass; I’m not stalking her."</i> ~Connor<br><br><u>Lines that punched me in the gut</u> <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br><br>"She lived for the days when it was only hands.” ~Tyler<br><br>“I never thought I’d live long enough to be able to move out of that house, so it seemed pointless to think about the future.” ~ Cassi<br>  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><br><br><a href="http://s1308.photobucket.com/albums/s607/aim4fashion/?action=view&amp;current=6688f920.png" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380390530i/752266.png" alt="Photobucket" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><u>My Thoughts</u><br>Mixed... A big mixed bag of emotions right now is what I feel. First I would like to make it clear that I will be reading more from this author. This book just was not for me. I could not comprehend all the miscommunication that went on between Gage and Cassi. It has to be the worse I have ever witnessed as a reader. How could they not once talk about how the feel and where to go from there for a whole goddamn year and a half. Who freaking does that??? Apparently them...<br> <br><b>My major issue???</b> -&gt; Story lines and consistency was off for me. And here is why.<br>The whole six month jump was kind of out of left field. I felt that the story should have been broken into three parts because the last 27% percent felt like a whole different book. And some of the character dynamics were effected due to this sudden shift. For instance Tyler, when his story lines pick back up he seems to have a whole 360 degree turnaround. He went from not wanting Gage and Cassi together to total acceptance in what seemed like over night.<br>Then you have two no, sorry, three new characters introduced in the last 30% of the book. Connor, Isabella and Jesse. Each play vital roles in the story. **Sighs heavily** Okay, so one was mentioned in the beginning however the other two are kinda just thrown in the mix. And that threw off some of the consistency in my humble opinion. However I could see where the author was going with the secondary love story and yes, I will read their book<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Jesse and Amanda ;) <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>Also there is a scene where Tyler and Cassi are talking and Gage overhears. Instead of confronting it head on by demanding answers he walks away.Huh..WTF... I felt that this was out of character for him especially when he is displayed as a alpha male with a temper whose quick to use his fist. Soooo, yeah some things felt off.<br><br> Dear readers,<br>I gave this book three stars because some of the story lines and character actions felt inconsistent. I thought the plot was pretty good and the steam was good too. I have seen a lot of mixed reviews for this book. If my review fails to provide insight then reading it is most likely the only way for you to know whether this is for you or not.<br><br>My Ratings<br>Characters- Love some, hate some <br>Writing Style- Fair/Passable<br>Storyline/Plot- Good, with some emotional turmoil and high drama<br>Steam Factor- High/Very Steamy<br>Overall- It was average. And I think I was expecting something different.<br><b><br>Now go forth and read. Then come tell us about it on Goodreads!</b><br><br>For more reviews got to <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://realitybites-letsgetlost.blogspot.com">http://realitybites-letsgetlost.blogs...</a> <br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/469399924" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/469399924?book_show_action=true">Dec 03, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jenny Levine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jenny Levine" href="/user/show/12673270-jenny-levine">Jenny Levine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer469399924" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer965567099999198127"><i> ...You had to find the beauty from the ashes.<br/>It didn’t take long for us to realize it didn’t just apply to actual ashes. Because there were a lot of times in our lives that we’d had to find the light in the dark. </i><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380399646ra/773588.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Yet again, another book I was disappointed with. Okay, I <u> LIKE </u> it. I didn't LOVE it. I'm going to be honest and say that this book annoyed the shit out of me, and finishing this one was a struggle. <i> Why? </i> Here's why.<br/><br/>*One word: <b> TYLER </b> --I wanna beat his ass to a pulp. <b> What.a.DOUCHE! </b></span>
  <span id="freeText965567099999198127" style="display:none"><i> ...You had to find the beauty from the ashes.<br>It didn’t take long for us to realize it didn’t just apply to actual ashes. Because there were a lot of times in our lives that we’d had to find the light in the dark. </i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380399646ra/773588.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Yet again, another book I was disappointed with. Okay, I <u> LIKE </u> it. I didn't LOVE it. I'm going to be honest and say that this book annoyed the shit out of me, and finishing this one was a struggle. <i> Why? </i> Here's why.<br><br>*One word: <b> TYLER </b> --I wanna beat his ass to a pulp. <b> What.a.DOUCHE! </b> Feeding wrong information on both Gage and Cassidy to keep them apart. Not cool dude. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ He even brought another girl to fvck because Cass doesn't want to do it, and then kicked Cass out of the house  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <i> GRRR! </i> He did redeem himself, but Idk if he should be forgiven that easy 'cause of all the trouble he'd caused. Tsk.<br><br><b> *The usage of the word <i> Y'ALL </i> </b> --This word is mentioned like a hundred times in the book. Okay, I get it. They're from Texas. Uh, whatever. I'm just annoyed I can't keep it outta my head. Like, I keep saying it. If it's a song, it's like I'm having <i> "Last Song Syndrome" </i> LOL. Am I the only one seeing this as a problem? (Okay, don't mind me *grins*)<br><br><b> *Nobody in this book freakin' <u> TALKS! </u> </b> --You see guys, talking is very important, y'all just assume everything. And it took years for them to sort out their problems, which I don't find realistic at all. I'm not really a fan of drama so imagine my frustration when this book has lots of 'em! Hell! Like 80% of it.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380399646ra/773589.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>So, the story was infuriating at the first 40%, but it gets better at 43% when <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ They confessed their feelings for each other!!! --&gt; <i> “I’m madly in love with you.”<br>My eyes grew even wider as I let that sink in.<br>“I’ve tried to keep my feelings to myself, and I know I’m no good at it, but I can’t keep doing it anymore. I don’t just view you as a friend,<br>Cass. I never have. I thought you should know. I know you don’t feel the same but I’m tired of lying and hiding it from you.” </i> And they both figured out Tyler's shit. *fist pumps*  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>That's just short lived. After that, Tyler strikes back, which results to another misunderstanding. I swear, it's neverending.<br><br>I <b> LOVE </b> Gage and Cassidy together though. And the secondary characters. The good thing about this book though is that this time, we'll get our HEA. The last chapters of this book are the best part <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ the wedding, Cassidy's near-death experience, her pregnancy  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> with the exception of Connor, another guy who Cass gets involved with. I don't think creating his character is necessary. It just confuses the readers as to whether or not she'll really end up with Gage. I mean, I'd had enough of the love triangle that is Tyler-Cass-Gage, so, NO, JUST <b> <u> NO.</u> </b><br><br>The epilogue was beautiful by the way.<br><br><b> Overall, </b> this was an <i> OKAY </i> read.<br><br><b> 3 STARS! </b></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
